## Ground Truth Analysis

## GT Analysis

The GT is:
$$f(P) = 0.845(-1 + P/5.115)(1 - P/34.44)P + 0.845(1 - e^{-0.0969P})P$$

Note: **The GT has no dependence on t**. This is critical.

Let me expand the first term:
$$0.845(-1 + P/5.115)(1 - P/34.44)P$$

Let me denote $a = 1/5.115$, $b = 1/34.44$. Then:
$$0.845(aP - 1)(1 - bP)P = 0.845(aP - abP^2 - 1 + bP)P$$
$$= 0.845(aP^2 - abP^3 - P + bP^2)$$
$$= 0.845(-abP^3 + (a+b)P^2 - P)$$

The second term: $0.845(1 - e^{-0.0969P})P = 0.845P - 0.845Pe^{-0.0969P}$

So GT = $0.845(-abP^3 + (a+b)P^2 - P) + 0.845P - 0.845Pe^{-0.0969P}$
$= -0.845abP^3 + 0.845(a+b)P^2 - 0.845P + 0.845P - 0.845Pe^{-0.0969P}$
$= -0.845abP^3 + 0.845(a+b)P^2 - 0.845Pe^{-0.0969P}$

So the GT is a **cubic polynomial in P** plus a term $P \cdot e^{-cP}$ (with negative exponent). The GT has **no t dependence**.

The basis functions needed are: $P^3$, $P^2$, $P \cdot e^{-cP}$ (and possibly $P$ and constant terms that could be zero).

Now let me check each candidate. I'll first eliminate candidates with t-dependence that can't be zeroed out, then check structural compatibility.

The GT is: $c_0(-c_1 + P/c_2)(c_3 - P/c_4)P + c_5(c_6 - e^{-c_7 P})P$

With the given constants, this simplifies to:
$0.845 \cdot \frac{(P - 5.115)(34.44 - P)}{5.115 \times 34.44} \cdot P + 0.845(1 - e^{-0.0969P})P$

The key structural elements are:
1. A cubic polynomial in P (from the first term)
2. $P \cdot e^{-cP}$ (from the second term)
3. No t-dependence

For a candidate to match, it must:
- Have no t-dependence (or be able to zero it out)
- Contain $P \cdot e^{cP}$ as a basis function (with c < 0)
- Be able to produce a cubic polynomial in P

Let me now systematically check which candidates have $P \cdot e^{cP}$:

Looking through all 80 candidates... None of them have an explicit $P \cdot e^{cP}$ term.

Some have $e^{cP}$ (candidates 1, 3, 5, 9, 17, 18, 19, 20, 21, 22, 23, 27, 28, 29, 31, 33, 34, 35, 39, 40, 41, 48, 50, 51, 52, 53, 54, 55, 59, 67).

Some have $\frac{P \cdot e^{cP}}{Pc_1+c_2}$ (candidate 58).

But $\frac{Pe^{cP}}{aP+b}$ is NOT the same as $Pe^{cP}$ - they differ by a rational factor.

Wait, let me look at candidate 58 more carefully:

**Candidate 58**: $\frac{Pc_0}{Pc_1+c_2} + \frac{Pc_3 e^{Pc_4}}{Pc_1+c_2} + \frac{Pc_5}{Pc_1+c_2} + \frac{c_6 e^{Pc_4}}{Pc_1+c_2} + \frac{c_7}{Pc_1+c_2} + \frac{c_8}{Pc_1+c_2}$

$= \frac{P(c_0+c_5) + (Pc_3+c_6)e^{Pc_4} + c_7+c_8}{Pc_1+c_2}$

This is $\frac{\text{polynomial} + (Pc_3+c_6)e^{Pc_4}}{Pc_1+c_2}$. 

If I set $c_1 = 0$ (making denominator just $c_2$), then:
$= \frac{P(c_0+c_5) + (Pc_3+c_6)e^{Pc_4} + c_7+c_8}{c_2}$
$= \frac{c_0+c_5}{c_2}P + \frac{c_3}{c_2}Pe^{Pc_4} + \frac{c_6}{c_2}e^{Pc_4} + \frac{c_7+c_8}{c_2}$

This gives: $AP + BPe^{cP} + De^{cP} + E$

The GT needs: $\alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \gamma Pe^{-\delta P}$

This candidate has $Pe^{cP}$ (good!) but also $e^{cP}$ (with the same exponent coefficient) and only linear polynomial terms (no $P^3$ or $P^2$).

The $e^{cP}$ term can't be zeroed without also zeroing $Pe^{cP}$ (they share the same $c_4$). Well, I can set $c_6 = 0$ to eliminate the pure $e^{cP}$ term. Then:
$AP + BPe^{cP} + E$

But I still need $P^3 + P^2$ and only have $P$ and a constant. **NO MATCH**.

Hmm, what if $c_1 \neq 0$? Then the denominator is $c_1 P + c_2$, and the expression becomes more complex. Let me think...

$\frac{(c_0+c_5)P + (c_3 P + c_6)e^{c_4 P} + (c_7+c_8)}{c_1 P + c_2}$

This doesn't simplify to polynomial + $Pe^{cP}$ for any choice of constants. **NO MATCH**.

Now let me reconsider. Is there ANY candidate that can produce both a cubic polynomial AND $Pe^{-cP}$?

Actually, I realize I should look at this differently. Some candidates combine rational functions with exponentials. A rational function $\frac{P^n \cdot \text{stuff}}{P \cdot c + d}$ can produce polynomials when the numerator degree exceeds denominator degree.

But I need $Pe^{cP}$ as well, and none of the candidates seem to have this.

Let me double-check by looking at candidates with both polynomial-generating capability and exponential terms:

**Candidate 76**: $\frac{P^2 c_0 + Pc_3 + Pc_4 + Pc_5\log(Pc_6+1) + Pc_7 + c_8\log(Pc_6+1)}{Pc_1+c_2}$

This has $P\log(cP+1)/(aP+b)$ and $\log(cP+1)/(aP+b)$ terms. No exponential. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 74**: $\frac{Pc_0 + Pc_3\log(Pc_4+1) + c_5\log(Pc_4+1)}{Pc_1+c_2}$

No exponential. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 75**: Similar to 74. **NO MATCH**.

I'm becoming increasingly convinced that none of the candidates can match the GT, because the GT requires $Pe^{-cP}$ as a basis function, and no candidate provides this.

But wait - let me reconsider whether the GT could be rewritten without $Pe^{cP}$.

GT = $0.845(-1 + P/5.115)(1 - P/34.44)P + 0.845(1 - e^{-0.0969P})P$

Could this be rewritten as a rational function + something simpler? No, because $e^{-cP}$ is transcendental and can't be expressed as a rational function.

Could $Pe^{-cP}$ be expressed as $e^{-cP + \ln P}$? Yes, but that doesn't help match any candidate structure.

Let me reconsider candidates that have both rational functions of P and exponentials, where the rational function could absorb the polynomial part:

For the GT, the polynomial part is:
$-0.845 \cdot \frac{1}{5.115 \times 34.44} P^3 + 0.845 \cdot (\frac{1}{5.115} + \frac{1}{34.44}) P^2 + 0.845P - 0.845P$

Wait, let me recompute:
$0.845(-1 + P/5.115)(1 - P/34.44)P$
$= 0.845(P/5.115 - 1)(1 - P/34.44)P$
$= 0.845[(P/5.115)(1) - (P/5.115)(P/34.44) - 1 + P/34.44]P$
$= 0.845[P/5.115 - P^2/(5.115 \times 34.44) - 1 + P/34.44]P$
$= 0.845[P^2/5.115 - P^3/(5.115 \times 34.44) - P + P^2/34.44]$

And $0.845(1 - e^{-0.0969P})P = 0.845P - 0.845Pe^{-0.0969P}$

Total GT = $0.845[-P^3/(5.115 \times 34.44) + P^2(1/5.115 + 1/34.44) - P + P - Pe^{-0.0969P}]$
$= 0.845[-P^3/(5.115 \times 34.44) + P^2(1/5.115 + 1/34.44) - Pe^{-0.0969P}]$

So GT = $aP^3 + bP^2 + cPe^{dP}$ where $a < 0$, $b > 0$, $c < 0$, $d < 0$.

This confirms: the GT requires $P^3$, $P^2$, and $Pe^{dP}$ as basis functions.

Now, I need to find candidates that can produce ALL THREE of these basis functions.

For $P^3$: Need either explicit $P^3$ term, or a rational function with numerator degree ≥ denominator degree + 3.

For $Pe^{dP}$: Need explicit $Pe^{cP}$ term.

I don't see any candidate with $Pe^{cP}$. Let me look one more time...

Actually, wait. Let me reconsider candidates with $P/(P c_1 + c_2)$ combined with $e^{cP}$. 

If I have $\frac{AP + B}{CP + D} + Ee^{FP}$, this equals $\frac{A}{C} + \frac{B - AD/C}{CP+D} + Ee^{FP}$.

This is: constant + simple_fraction + exponential. This can NEVER equal $aP^3 + bP^2 + cPe^{dP}$.

What about candidates with $P \cdot c_0 + \frac{stuff}{Pc_1+c_2} + e^{cP}$?

$Pc_0 + \frac{Pc_3+c_8}{Pc_1+c_2} + c_4 e^{Pc_5}$

This is: linear + rational + exponential. Still can't produce cubic or $Pe^{cP}$.

What about $P^2 c_0 + Pc_1 + \frac{stuff}{Pc_3+c_4} + c_5 e^{Pc_6}$ (Candidate 31)?

Quadratic + linear + rational + exponential. Missing $P^3$ and has $e^{cP}$ instead of $Pe^{cP}$.

I'm now quite confident that **none of the candidates can match the GT**.

But let me do one final check. Could any candidate with $\log(cP+1)$ work? We know $\log(cP+1)$ is NOT equivalent to $Pe^{dP}$ for any constants. So no.

Could any candidate with $\sin(cP+d)$ work? $\sin$ is periodic and bounded, while $Pe^{dP}$ is not (for $d > 0$) or decays (for $d < 0$). Not equivalent.

Could $P^c$ (power function) work? $P^c$ for non-integer $c$ is a different basis function from $Pe^{dP}$.

Let me also verify: could the GT be rewritten as a rational function? No, because it contains $e^{-cP}$.

Let me verify one more time that the GT truly has no t-dependence. Looking at the GT: $c_0(-c_1 + P/c_2)(c_3 - P/c_4)P + c_5(c_6 - \exp(-c_7 P))P$. Yes, no t anywhere.

So any candidate with unavoidable t-dependence is automatically out, and any candidate without t but lacking $Pe^{cP}$ is also out.

Let me verify my conclusion by checking a few more candidates carefully:

**Candidate 20**: $\frac{Pc_0+Pc_3+c_8}{Pc_1+c_2} + c_4\log(Pc_5+1) + c_6 e^{Pc_7}$

No t. Has rational + log + exp. Basis functions: constant, $\frac{1}{aP+b}$, $\log(cP+1)$, $e^{dP}$. None of these are $P^3$, $P^2$, or $Pe^{eP}$. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 23**: $\frac{Pc_0+Pc_3+c_8+c_9}{Pc_1+c_2} + c_4\log(Pc_5+1) + c_6 e^{Pc_7}$

Same as 20 with one more constant in numerator. Same basis functions. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 21**: $\frac{Pc_0+c_7+c_8}{Pc_1+c_2} + c_3\log(Pc_4+1) + c_5 e^{Pc_6}$

Same structure. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 38**: $\frac{Pc_0+Pc_4+c_8}{Pc_1+c_2} + Pc_3 + c_5\log(Pc_6+1) + c_7$

Has $Pc_3$ (linear) + rational + log + constant. No exponential at all. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 43**: $\frac{Pc_0+Pc_4+c_7+c_8}{Pc_1+c_2} + Pc_3 + c_5\log(Pc_6+1)$

Linear + rational + log. No exponential. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 44**: $\frac{Pc_0+Pc_4+c_8}{Pc_1+c_2} + Pc_3 + P^{c_5}c_6 + c_7$

Linear + rational + power + constant. No exponential. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 65**: $\frac{Pc_0}{P+c_1} + Pc_2 + \frac{Pc_3+c_6}{Pc_4+c_1} + c_5$

If $c_4=1$, both denominators are $P+c_1$: $\frac{Pc_0+Pc_3+c_6}{P+c_1} + Pc_2 + c_5$. This is linear + rational + constant. No exponential. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 66**: $\frac{Pc_0+Pc_4}{Pc_1+c_2} + Pc_3 + c_5 + \frac{c_6}{P+c_2}$

Note different denominators: $Pc_1+c_2$ and $P+c_2$. If $c_1=1$: $\frac{Pc_0+Pc_4+c_6}{P+c_2} + Pc_3 + c_5$. Linear + rational + constant. **NO MATCH**.

I've now checked all candidates and none of them contain the $Pe^{cP}$ basis function needed to match the GT.

Actually, wait. Let me reconsider one more time. What if I'm wrong about the GT requiring $Pe^{cP}$? Let me re-examine.

GT = $0.845(-1 + P/5.115)(1 - P/34.44)P + 0.845(1 - e^{-0.0969P})P$

The second term is $0.845P - 0.845Pe^{-0.0969P}$. The $0.845P$ is a polynomial term. The $-0.845Pe^{-0.0969P}$ is indeed $Pe^{cP}$ with $c = -0.0969$.

This is a fundamental basis function that cannot be decomposed into simpler standard functions. So yes, the GT requires $Pe^{cP}$.

Since no candidate has this basis function, none can match.

But wait - I should double-check my analysis. Let me re-examine candidate 58 with $c_1 = 0$:

$\frac{c_0+c_5}{c_2}P + \frac{c_3}{c_2}Pe^{c_4 P} + \frac{c_6}{c_2}e^{c_4 P} + \frac{c_7+c_8}{c_2}$

This HAS $Pe^{c_4 P}$! And it has $P$ (linear), $e^{c_4 P}$, and a constant.

But the GT needs $P^3 + P^2 + Pe^{cP}$. This candidate (with $c_1=0$) gives $P + Pe^{cP} + e^{cP} + \text{const}$.

Can I set $c_6 = 0$ to eliminate $e^{cP}$? Yes: $AP + BPe^{cP} + E$.

But I still need $P^3$ and $P^2$, and I only have $P$ and constant. So this doesn't work.

Unless... what if $c_1 \neq 0$? Then the denominator is $c_1 P + c_2$, and:

$\frac{(c_0+c_5)P + (c_3 P + c_6)e^{c_4 P} + (c_7+c_8)}{c_1 P + c_2}$

This is a complicated expression. Let me see if it could equal $aP^3 + bP^2 + cPe^{dP}$.

$(aP^3 + bP^2 + cPe^{dP})(c_1 P + c_2) = (c_0+c_5)P + (c_3 P + c_6)e^{c_4 P} + (c_7+c_8)$

LHS: $ac_1 P^4 + (ac_2 + bc_1)P^3 + bc_2 P^2 + cc_1 P^2 e^{dP} + cc_2 Pe^{dP}$

RHS: $(c_0+c_5)P + c_3 Pe^{c_4 P} + c_6 e^{c_4 P} + (c_7+c_8)$

For these to be equal:
- $P^4$ coefficient: $ac_1 = 0$. Since $a \neq 0$ (GT has cubic term), $c_1 = 0$.

So we're back to $c_1 = 0$, which gives us only linear + $Pe^{cP}$ + $e^{cP}$ + constant. Not enough polynomial terms.

**Candidate 58 verdict: NO MATCH**.

OK so my conclusion stands. Let me now formally go through each candidate:

For ALL candidates: The GT requires the basis function $Pe^{cP}$ (specifically $Pe^{-0.0969P}$). This function cannot be produced by:
- Rational functions of P
- Pure exponentials $e^{cP}$
- Logarithms $\log(cP+1)$
- Trigonometric functions $\sin(cP+d)$
- Power functions $P^c$
- Any finite combination of the above

The only candidate that has $Pe^{cP}$ in any form is Candidate 58, but when $c_1=0$ (the only way to extract $Pe^{cP}$), it lacks the necessary $P^3$ and $P^2$ terms.

Additionally, the GT requires $P^3$ and $P^2$ polynomial terms, which most candidates also cannot produce.

Therefore, no candidate matches the GT.

Wait, actually I want to reconsider one more time. Let me look at candidates that have both $P^2$ terms AND exponentials, even if they don't have $Pe^{cP}$.

Actually, I realize I should also check: could ANY combination of the available basis functions in a candidate exactly equal $Pe^{-cP}$ for all P ≥ 0? The answer is definitively no, because:

1. $Pe^{-cP}$ is not a rational function
2. $Pe^{-cP}$ is not $e^{aP}$ for any $a$
3. $Pe^{-cP}$ is not $\log(aP+1)$ for any $a$
4. $Pe^{-cP}$ is not any finite sum of the above

This is a consequence of the linear independence of these function families.

So my final answer is that no candidate matches.

Actually, hold on. Let me reconsider candidates 29, 39, 40, 41 which have both $Pc_0$ (standalone linear P term) and rational functions and exponentials. Could combining $Pc_0$ with $\frac{stuff}{Pc_1+c_2}$ give higher-order polynomials? 

$Pc_0 + \frac{Pc_1' + c_8}{Pc_2' + c_3'} = \frac{c_0 c_2' P^2 + (c_0 c_3' + c_1')P + c_8}{c_2' P + c_3'}$

This is a quadratic over linear, which gives linear + constant + fraction. So no $P^3$.

What about $P^2 c_0 + Pc_1 + \frac{stuff}{Pc_3+c_4}$ (Candidate 31)?

$P^2 c_0 + Pc_1 + \frac{Pc_2+c_7+c_8}{Pc_3+c_4} + c_5 e^{Pc_6}$

This has $P^2$ (quadratic), $P$ (linear), rational (constant + fraction), and $e^{cP}$. Missing $P^3$ and $Pe^{cP}$. **NO MATCH**.

I'm confident now. Let me write up the verdicts.
